The Mu'tazilite Criterion for Distinguishing Attributes
Mu'tazilite criterion for distinguishing attribute types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite criterion for distinguishing between attributes of essence and attributes of action, and why it leads to classifying speech as an act-attribute.

Core Idea
If an attribute can be negated, it is an act-attribute, not an essence-attribute.

The disagreement over kalam leads to the need for a clear criterion to distinguish between eternal and temporal attributes. The Mu'tazila propose a specific logical test: an attribute of the essence is one that cannot be negated without contradiction. They apply this test to knowledge, power, sight, and hearing, which all pass as essence-attributes. But when applied to speech, they argue it can be negated, placing it among act-attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the criterion passage
Read the Arabic text defining the distinguishing boundary (al-hadd al-fasil).
2
Understand the test
The test is: if an attribute can be affirmed with no possible negation, it is of the essence.
3
Examine the examples
Look at the examples given for knowledge, power, sight, hearing.
4
Apply to kalam
Consider why the Mu'tazila think kalam does not pass this test—because they believe it can be negated (He was not speaking in pre-eternity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The criterion that 'what cannot be negated is an essence-attribute' is universally accepted by all theologians.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite criterion, why is speech (kalam) considered an attribute of action rather than of the essence?

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite criterion for distinguishing attributes is whether negating the attribute is permissible; this leads them to classify speech as an act-attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Could it be that your comfort with a particular view of God's attributes is more about your own need for certainty than about the evidence? What would it cost you to genuinely consider that God's speech is an act?
?
If you were to apply the Mu'tazilite criterion to your own understanding of God, which of His attributes would you most resist classifying as an act-attribute? Why does that resistance reveal about what you feel you need God to be—rather than what He has revealed Himself to be?
?
The Mu'tazila required that an attribute of essence cannot be negated. In your prayer life, do you ever act as if God's hearing or seeing can be negated—by forgetting that He sees your secret deeds or hears your silent thoughts? How can you live today in the constant awareness that His seeing and hearing are never absent?

The Mu'tazili Criterion for Distinguishing Divine Attributes
Nasafi presents the agreement and the Mu'tazila's first criterion for distinguishing essential from active attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial agreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Hadith on divine attributes, the point of disagreement regarding speech, and the Mu'tazila's first criterion for distinguishing essential from active attributes.

Core Idea
Essential attributes are eternally affirmed; active attributes are temporally realized.

This passage from Nasafi's work presents a pivotal moment in the theological debate on divine attributes. It shows where the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Hadith agree and where they differ, especially on the nature of speech. The Mu'tazila then propose a logical criterion to determine which attributes belong to essence and which to action, a criterion that has implications for the eternity of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall flow.
Notice the structure: agreement, disagreement, criterion, application.
2
Identify the agreement and disagreement
Find where the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Hadith agree (essential attributes eternal, active temporal) and where they differ (speech).
The consensus is on attributes like life, power, knowledge; the dispute is on speech.
3
Understand the Mu'tazili criterion
The Mu'tazila propose that attributes that cannot be negated of God are essential; those that can be negated in specific instances are active. See the examples with knowing, hearing vs. creating, speaking.
This criterion is used to classify speech as an active attribute.
4
Reflect on the consequence for speech
Since speech can be negated (e.g., God did not speak to Pharaoh), it is considered an active attribute, thus not eternal. This leads to the Mu'tazili position that the Quran is created.
The passage ends with a note about Ibn Haytham's mistaken attribution of this criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت الخصوم: إن ما كان من صفات الذات فهو أزلي وما كان من صفات الفعل فهو حادث فعلى هذا انعقد الإجماع بين المعتزلة وبين متكلمي أهل الحديث، أنه تعالى كان في الأزل حيا باقيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا وأنه لم يكن خالقا ولا رازقا ولا مصورا ولا محيبا ولا مميتا، لأن القسم الأول من صفات الذات والقسم الثاني من صفات الفعل، واختلفوا أنه تعالى هل كان في الأزل متكلما؟ فقال أهل الحديث : كان متكلماً فى الأزل؛ لأن الكلام من قبيل صفات الذات. وقالت المعتزلة : لم يكن في الأزل متكلما ، لأن الكلام من صفات الفعل. وتفرع من هذا اختلاف فيما بينهم في الحد الفاصل بين صفات الذات وصفات الفعل ففرقت المعتزلة بينهما فرقا يبقى الكلام في جملة صفات الفعل فقالت: الفرق بينهما أن ما يثبت ولا يجوز نفيه فهو من صفات الذات، فإنه يقال: يعلم كذا، ولا يقال لا يعلم كذا وكذا يقال يقدر على كذا، ولا يقال لا يقدر على كذا ، ويقال : يبصر فلانا، ولا يقال لا يبصر فلانا، وكذا يقال : يسمع صوت فلان، ولا يقال لا يسمع صوت فلان. ثم يقال : إنه تعالى خلق لزيد ولدا ولم يخلق لعمر ، ورزق عبد الله مالاً ولم يرزق خالدا فدل أن الفرق هو هذا ثم يصح أن يقال: إنه تعالى كلم موسى عليه السلام ولم يكلم فرعون ، دل أنه من قبيل صفات الفعل. فلم يكن الله تعالى موصوفا به في الأزل. ونسب ابن هيضم من جملة الكرامية هذا الفرق إلى عبد الله بن سعيد القطان المعروف بابن كلاب وإلى الأشعري جهلا منه بمذاهب خصومه.
And the opponents said: Indeed, whatever is from the attributes of essence is eternal, and whatever is from the attributes of action is temporal. Upon this, consensus was established between the Mu'tazila and the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith that God, exalted, was in pre-eternity living, enduring, powerful, knowing, hearing, seeing, and that He was not a creator, nor a provider, nor a fashioner, nor a giver of life, nor a giver of death, because the first division is from the attributes of essence and the second division is from the attributes of action. And they differed about whether God, exalted, was in pre-eternity speaking. Ahl al-Hadith said: He was speaking in pre-eternity, because speech is from the category of attributes of essence. The Mu'tazila said: He was not in pre-eternity speaking, because speech is from the attributes of action. And from this branched a difference among them regarding the distinguishing boundary between attributes of essence and attributes of action. So the Mu'tazila distinguished between them with a distinction that keeps speech within the category of attributes of action. They said: The distinction between them is that what is affirmed and whose negation is not permissible is from the attributes of essence. For it is said: He knows such and such, and it is not said: He does not know such and such. Likewise it is said: He is able to do such and such, and it is not said: He is not able to do such and such. And it is said: He sees so-and-so, and it is not said: He does not see so-and-so. Similarly, it is said: He hears the voice of so-and-so, and it is not said: He does not hear the voice of so-and-so. Then it is said: Indeed, God, exalted, created a son for Zayd and did not create for 'Amr, and provided 'Abdullah with wealth and did not provide Khalid. So that indicates that the distinction is this. Then it is valid to say: Indeed, God, exalted, spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, and did not speak to Pharaoh. This indicates that it is from the category of attributes of action. So God, exalted, was not described with it in pre-eternity. And Ibn Haytham, from among the Karramiyya, attributed this distinction to 'Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan known as Ibn Kullab and to al-Ash'ari, out of ignorance of the doctrines of his opponents.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage defines the initial agreement between the Mu'tazila and the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith on the classification of divine attributes as eternal or temporal, then presents the first Mu'tazili criterion for distinguishing between attributes of essence and attributes of action. The author begins by stating that both groups agree that essential attributes (like life, power, knowledge, hearing, sight) are eternal, while active attributes (like creating, providing, fashioning, giving life, giving death) are temporal. However, they differ on speech: Ahl al-Hadith consider speech an eternal attribute of essence, while the Mu'tazila consider it a temporal attribute of action. This disagreement leads to a deeper examination of the distinguishing criterion. The Mu'tazila propose that whatever can be affirmed and cannot be negated is an attribute of essence; the negation would be impossible. For example, one can say 'He knows' but not 'He does not know', and similarly for power, seeing, hearing. In contrast, attributes that can be negated in specific instances are active attributes, such as creating a child for one person but not another, or speaking to Moses but not to Pharaoh. Since these actions are contingent and not necessary, they are not eternal. The passage concludes with a note that Ibn Haytham from the Karramiyya incorrectly attributed this very distinction to Ibn Kullab and al-Ash'ari, showing his ignorance of the doctrines of his opponents.

Misconception: One might think the Mu'tazila deny all eternal attributes.
Correction: The Mu'tazila affirm essential attributes like life, power, and knowledge as eternal; they only deny the eternity of active attributes like speech.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila distinguished essential attributes as those that cannot be negated of God, while active attributes can be negated in particular instances, making speech an active attribute.

Examine your heart: do you read the Qur'an as a timeless address from an eternally speaking God, or as a temporal message that might not be directly for you? Commit to reading a verse today as if God is speaking it to you right now.
?
Ibn Haytham confidently attributed a view to Ibn Kullab and al-Ash'ari out of ignorance. Have you ever been sure you understood someone's position, only to later realize you were mistaken? How can this lesson help you cultivate humility in theological discussions? This week, before labeling someone's belief, will you pause to verify from their own works what they actually hold?

The Mu'tazili criterion tests an attribute by whether it can be negated. In your own life, do you treat God's attributes as always true or do you sometimes act as if He does not see or hear you? Reflect on a moment you sinned in private: did you truly believe God sees and hears at that moment? If not, what does that reveal about your heart's affirmation of His essential attributes? Make a concrete commitment to remind yourself daily of one essential attribute and its implications for your conduct.

Second Mu'tazili Criterion: The Opposite Test
Nasafi explains the second Mu'tazili criterion using opposite pairs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila use the criterion of whether an attribute's opposite can be described of God to distinguish essential attributes from active attributes.

Core Idea
If an attribute's opposite is never said of God, it is essential; if both are said, it is active.

The Mu'tazila developed several criteria to classify divine attributes. One of their key tests looks at whether the opposite of a given attribute can be truthfully predicated of God. If God can be described with both an attribute and its opposite (in different contexts), it is an attribute of action. If only one side is possible, it is an attribute of essence. In this passage, Nasafi presents this second criterion and illustrates it with clear examples from the Qur'anic descriptions of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Nasafi states the criterion and then lists examples.
The criterion is given in the first sentence.
2
Identify the pairs of opposites
Make a list of the opposite pairs mentioned: life/death, power/incapacity, knowledge/ignorance, etc. Separate them into two groups: those where only one side applies to God, and those where both sides apply.
The essential attributes are those whose opposite is never attributed to God.
3
Understand the logic
Ask yourself: why does the possibility of opposite attribution indicate an attribute of action? Because actions vary with circumstances, whereas essence is unchanging.
This criterion reflects the Mu'tazili view that God's actions are multiple and contingent.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice the final sentence: the ability to describe God with commanding and forbidding, prohibiting and obligating, shows these are attributes of action. This is the inferential step: from the possibility of opposites to the classification as act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما يقولون ما يوصف به ولا يوصف بضده فهو من صفات الذات، فإنه يوصف بالحياة ولا يوصف بالموت، وكذا في القدرة والعجز والعلم والجهل والبصر والعمى والسمع والصم. ويوصف بالإحياء والإماتة والتحريك والتسكين والتسويد والتبييض. ثم هو يوصف بالأمر والنهي والحظر والإيجاب ودل أنه من صفات الفعل.
And sometimes they say: What is described with it and whose opposite is not described is from the attributes of essence. For He is described with life and is not described with death, and similarly in power and incapacity, knowledge and ignorance, sight and blindness, hearing and deafness. And He is described with giving life and giving death, moving and stilling, blackening and whitening. Then He is described with commanding and forbidding, prohibiting and obligating, and that indicates that it is from the attributes of action.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage presents a second criterion used by the Mu'tazila to distinguish between attributes of essence and attributes of action. The criterion focuses on whether the opposite of an attribute can be attributed to God. If an attribute is such that its opposite cannot be described of God at all, then it is an attribute of essence. For example, God is described with life, but cannot be described with death; similarly for power (not incapacity), knowledge (not ignorance), sight (not blindness), hearing (not deafness). These are essential attributes. In contrast, attributes like giving life and giving death can both be attributed to God depending on the situation; likewise moving and stilling, blackening and whitening, commanding and forbidding, prohibiting and obligating. Since both the attribute and its opposite can be described of God in different contexts, these are attributes of action. The passage concludes that this distinction shows that such attributes (like commanding, forbidding, etc.) are active attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if an attribute has an opposite, it must be an active attribute, regardless of whether the opposite is ever attributed to God.
Correction: The Mu'tazila distinguish: essential attributes are those whose opposite is never attributed to God (e.g., life without death), while active attributes can have both the attribute and its opposite attributed to God in different contexts (e.g., giving life and giving death).

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili criterion of opposite attribution helps classify attributes: essential if opposite impossible, active if both possible.

?
This passage shows that the Mu'tazila insisted on logical consistency in divine attributes. In what area of your own belief do you hesitate to apply such rigorous reasoning? What fear holds you back?
?
The fact that God can be described with both 'commanding' and 'forbidding' shows His active will in our lives. Reflect on a situation where you struggled to accept God's command or prohibition. How does knowing that both come from the same perfect will change your trust in Him?

Ahl al-Hadith Criterion: Deficiency Upon Negation
Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Hadith's criterion for essential vs. active attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Hadith criterion for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of action, based on whether negation implies a deficiency.

Core Idea
Negation reveals essence: if denying it implies a flaw, it's essential.

How can we tell which of God's attributes are essential and which are acts? The Ahl al-Hadith propose a simple test: if denying the attribute would suggest a shortcoming in God, then it must be an attribute of His essence. This lesson presents their criterion and its application.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the structure: the criterion is stated first, then examples for essential attributes, then examples for active attributes.
The passage is concise; each example illustrates the logic.
2
Identify the criterion
Find the phrase 'ما يلزم بنفيه نقيصة' and understand it as the defining test. Any attribute whose negation entails a deficiency (like death, incapacity, ignorance, etc.) is an attribute of essence.
The criterion applies only to attributes of essence (sifat al-dhat), not attributes of action.
3
Examine the examples for essence
Notice the pairs: life/death, power/incapacity, knowledge/ignorance, sight/blindness, hearing/deafness. Each pair shows that denying the positive implies the negative deficiency.
These are all perfections that God must have; their absence would be a flaw.
4
Examine the examples for action
Now look at the examples of active attributes: giving life, giving death, moving, stilling. Denying these does not imply a deficiency because God may simply not do them at a given time without flaw.
Attributes of action are contingent; they do not affect God's perfection.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters: it helps categorize divine attributes and avoid attributing temporality or change to God's essence.
This criterion is specific to Ahl al-Hadith; other schools (like the Mu'tazila or Maturidis) may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومتكلمو أهل الحديث يفرقون بينهما بفرق، يبقى الكلام في جملة صفات الذات دون صفات الفعل فيقولون : ما يلزم بنفيه نقيصة فهو من صفات الذات، فإنك لو نفيت الحياة يلزم نقيصة الموت، ولو نفيت القدرة يلزم نقيصة العجز، وكذا هذا في العلم والجهل، والبصر مع العمى، والسمع ومع الصم. وما لا يلزم بنفيه نقيصة فهو من صفات الفعل فإنك لو نفيت عنه الإحياء أو الإماتة أو التحريك أو التسكين لم يلزم نقيصة . عرف أن الفرق بينهما هذا.
And the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith distinguish between them with a distinction that keeps speech within the category of attributes of essence and not attributes of action. They say: What, by its negation, entails a deficiency is from the attributes of essence. For if you negate life, the deficiency of death is entailed; if you negate power, the deficiency of incapacity is entailed; likewise this in knowledge and ignorance, sight with blindness, hearing with deafness. And what, by its negation, does not entail a deficiency is from the attributes of action. For if you negate from Him giving life or giving death or moving or stilling, no deficiency is entailed. It is known that the distinction between them is this.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage presents the criterion of Ahl al-Hadith for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of action. The theologians of Ahl al-Hadith propose that if negating an attribute would imply a deficiency in God, then that attribute is an attribute of essence. For example, if you negate life, the deficiency of death is implied; similarly, negating power implies incapacity, negating knowledge implies ignorance, negating sight implies blindness, negating hearing implies deafness. Therefore, these attributes are essential—they must be affirmed for God's perfection. In contrast, attributes of action are those whose negation does not imply any deficiency. For instance, if you say God does not give life to a particular person or does not cause death at a certain time, or does not move or still something, no deficiency is attributed to God. Thus, these attributes are temporal and not necessary. The passage concludes that this is the recognized distinction according to Ahl al-Hadith.

الموت
العجز
الإحياء
الإماتة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that negating an active attribute like giving life is always a deficiency, but Ahl al-Hadith argue it is not, because God may choose not to give life to a specific being without it reflecting a flaw in His essence.
Correction: The criterion is specifically about deficiency in God's essence. Active attributes are contingent; their negation does not imply a flaw in God's nature.

Checkpoint

A) Because life is mentioned in the Quran
B) Because negating life would imply the deficiency of death
C) Because life is eternal
D) Because life is a perfection

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Hadith distinguish essential attributes from active ones by checking if negation entails a deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When was the last time you paused because you realized God sees you or hears you? What obstacle keeps you from that awareness—and what will you do about it today?
?
The passage says that negating an active attribute like giving life does not imply any deficiency in God. Does your soul truly trust that God's perfection does not depend on His specific actions? Or do you sometimes assume that if God doesn't act in a certain way (e.g., answer a prayer), He must be less powerful? How will you train your heart to submit to this truth?

Consider the attribute of knowledge: if God were ignorant, that would be a deficiency. Are there areas of your life where you act as if God does not know—perhaps in secret sin or hidden thoughts? This lesson calls you to affirm His perfect knowledge. What one specific action will you take today to align your behavior with the reality that God knows everything, even what you try to hide?

The First Criterion: Attributes Described with Their Opposites
Explains the first criterion based on opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first criterion used by some theologians to distinguish attributes of essence from attributes of action based on whether the attribute's opposite can be predicated of God.

Core Idea
If God is described by an attribute but not by its opposite, it is an attribute of essence.

The passage begins by illustrating that God speaking to Moses but not to Pharaoh shows speech is an attribute of action. It then attributes this type of reasoning to Ibn Kullab and al-Ash'ari, presenting a criterion: attributes of essence are those for which God is described by the attribute itself and not by its opposite. This lesson unpacks that criterion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the example of speech to Moses.
Why does the fact that God spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh indicate speech is an attribute of action?
The example shows that speech is something God does in time, not an eternal attribute.
2
Identify the criterion from Ibn Kullab.
The criterion is: what He is described by and its opposite is not described, that is an attribute of essence.
Note the list of pairs: life/death, power/incapacity, etc.
3
Contrast with attributes of action.
Attributes like giving life, causing death, etc., are described as actions because their opposites can also be described (e.g., He gives life and causes death).
These are pairs that can both be said of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فدل أن الفرق هو هذا ثم يصح أن يقال: إنه تعالى كلم موسى عليه السلام (۱) ولم يكلم فرعون دل أنه من قبيل صفات الفعل. فلم يكن الله تعالى موصوفا به في الأزل. ونسب ابن هيضم (۲) من جملة الكرامية هذا الفرق إلى عبد الله بن سعيد القطان المعروف بابن كلاب (۳) وإلى الأشعري جهلا منه بمذاهب خصومه، وربما يقولون ما يوصف به ولا يوصف بضده فهو من صفات الذات، فإنه يوصف بالحياة ولا يوصف بالموت، وكذا في القدرة والعجز والعلم والجهل والبصر والعمى والسمع والصم. ويوصف بالإحياء والإماتة والتحريك والتسكين والتسويد والتبييض. ثم هو يوصف بالأمر والنهي والحظر والإيجاب ودل أنه من صفات الفعل. ومتكلمو أهل الحديث يفرقون بينهما بفرق، يبقى الكلام في جملة صفات الذات دون صفات الفعل فيقولون: ما يلزم بنفيه نقيصة فهو من صفات الذات، فإنك لو نفيت الحياة يلزم نقيصة الموت، ولو نفيت القدرة يلزم نقيصة العجز، وكذا هذا في العلم والجهل، والبصر مع العمى، والسمع ومع الصم. وما لا يلزم بنفيه نقيصة فهو من صفات الفعل فإنك لو نفيت عنه الإحياء أو الإماتة أو التحريك أو التسكين لم يلزم نقيصة . عرف أن الفرق بينهما هذا . ثم لو نفى عنه الكلام للزمته نقيصة الآفة كالعجز والخرس فكان من صفات الذات
So it indicates that the distinction is this. Then it is correct to say: He, exalted, spoke to Moses (upon him peace) and did not speak to Pharaoh, indicating that it is of the category of attributes of action. So God, exalted, was not described by it in eternity. Ibn Haydam, from the Karramiyya, attributed this distinction to Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan known as Ibn Kullab and to al-Ash'ari, out of ignorance of the doctrines of his opponents. And perhaps they say: what He is described by and its opposite is not described, it is from the attributes of essence. For He is described by life and not described by death, and likewise in power and incapacity, knowledge and ignorance, sight and blindness, hearing and deafness. And He is described by giving life and causing death, moving and stilling, blackening and whitening. Then He is described by command and prohibition, restriction and obligation, and it indicates that it is from the attributes of action. The mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith distinguish between them by another distinction, keeping speech among the attributes of essence without the attributes of action. They say: what negation of it entails a defect is from the attributes of essence. For if you negate life, the defect of death is entailed; and if you negate power, the defect of incapacity is entailed; and likewise in knowledge and ignorance, sight with blindness, hearing with deafness. And what negation of it does not entail a defect is from the attributes of action. For if you negate giving life or causing death or moving or stilling, no defect is entailed. It is known that the distinction between them is this. Then if speech is negated from Him, the defect of impairment like incapacity and muteness would be entailed, so it is from the attributes of essence.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof. It presents two criteria used by different groups to distinguish between attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fiʿl). The first criterion is based on whether the attribute can be described along with its opposite: if an attribute is such that both it and its opposite cannot be described of God, it is an attribute of essence (e.g., life vs. death). If an attribute can be described but its opposite cannot, it is an attribute of action (e.g., giving life vs. giving death is not a true opposite). The second criterion, used by the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, is based on consequence: if negating the attribute entails a defect (naqīṣa) in God, it is an attribute of essence; if negation does not entail a defect, it is an attribute of action. The passage then applies this to divine speech (al-kalām): negating speech would entail the defect of incapacity or muteness, therefore speech is an attribute of essence.

صفات الفعل
ابن كلاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all attributes of God are eternal and unchanging, so speech must be an attribute of essence.
Correction: The passage shows that the ability to speak to one but not another indicates it is an action, not an eternal attribute.

Checkpoint

A) Giving life
B) Power
C) Command

Key Takeaway
The first criterion distinguishes essence and action based on whether the opposite can be described of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How does this criterion push you to rely solely on His unchanging essence rather than your fluctuating circumstances?

How comfortable are you with the full range of His actions, even the difficult ones? Will you thank Him today for both what He gives and what He withholds?
?
The passage mentions that God spoke to Moses but not to Pharaoh. Do you truly seek to hear God's speech (the Quran) as a personal address to you, or do you read it as a historical record? If God's speech is an attribute of action that targets certain individuals, how will you ensure you are among those He speaks to?

The Second Criterion: Negation and Defect
Explains the second criterion based on defect consequence and applies it to speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the criterion used by the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, which focuses on whether negating the attribute implies a defect in God.

Core Idea
If negating an attribute entails a defect, it is an attribute of essence; otherwise, it is an action.

The passage then presents a different criterion from the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith: they judge attributes by what happens if you negate them. If negation implies a deficiency (like death, ignorance), the attribute is essential; if not, it is an action. The passage applies this to speech, concluding it is essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the second criterion.
Identify the rule: 'ما يلزم بنفيه نقيصة فهو من صفات الذات'.
They give examples: negating life entails death, a defect.
2
Apply to attributes of action.
Negating actions like giving life does not entail a defect, so they are actions.
The absence of an action does not imply imperfection.
3
Apply to divine speech.
Negating speech would entail the defect of muteness, so speech is an attribute of essence.
This shows speech is essential, even though it was used as an example of action in the first criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فدل أن الفرق هو هذا ثم يصح أن يقال: إنه تعالى كلم موسى عليه السلام (۱) ولم يكلم فرعون دل أنه من قبيل صفات الفعل. فلم يكن الله تعالى موصوفا به في الأزل. ونسب ابن هيضم (۲) من جملة الكرامية هذا الفرق إلى عبد الله بن سعيد القطان المعروف بابن كلاب (۳) وإلى الأشعري جهلا منه بمذاهب خصومه، وربما يقولون ما يوصف به ولا يوصف بضده فهو من صفات الذات، فإنه يوصف بالحياة ولا يوصف بالموت، وكذا في القدرة والعجز والعلم والجهل والبصر والعمى والسمع والصم. ويوصف بالإحياء والإماتة والتحريك والتسكين والتسويد والتبييض. ثم هو يوصف بالأمر والنهي والحظر والإيجاب ودل أنه من صفات الفعل. ومتكلمو أهل الحديث يفرقون بينهما بفرق، يبقى الكلام في جملة صفات الذات دون صفات الفعل فيقولون: ما يلزم بنفيه نقيصة فهو من صفات الذات، فإنك لو نفيت الحياة يلزم نقيصة الموت، ولو نفيت القدرة يلزم نقيصة العجز، وكذا هذا في العلم والجهل، والبصر مع العمى، والسمع ومع الصم. وما لا يلزم بنفيه نقيصة فهو من صفات الفعل فإنك لو نفيت عنه الإحياء أو الإماتة أو التحريك أو التسكين لم يلزم نقيصة . عرف أن الفرق بينهما هذا . ثم لو نفى عنه الكلام للزمته نقيصة الآفة كالعجز والخرس فكان من صفات الذات
So it indicates that the distinction is this. Then it is correct to say: He, exalted, spoke to Moses (upon him peace) and did not speak to Pharaoh, indicating that it is of the category of attributes of action. So God, exalted, was not described by it in eternity. Ibn Haydam, from the Karramiyya, attributed this distinction to Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan known as Ibn Kullab and to al-Ash'ari, out of ignorance of the doctrines of his opponents. And perhaps they say: what He is described by and its opposite is not described, it is from the attributes of essence. For He is described by life and not described by death, and likewise in power and incapacity, knowledge and ignorance, sight and blindness, hearing and deafness. And He is described by giving life and causing death, moving and stilling, blackening and whitening. Then He is described by command and prohibition, restriction and obligation, and it indicates that it is from the attributes of action. The mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith distinguish between them by another distinction, keeping speech among the attributes of essence without the attributes of action. They say: what negation of it entails a defect is from the attributes of essence. For if you negate life, the defect of death is entailed; and if you negate power, the defect of incapacity is entailed; and likewise in knowledge and ignorance, sight with blindness, hearing with deafness. And what negation of it does not entail a defect is from the attributes of action. For if you negate giving life or causing death or moving or stilling, no defect is entailed. It is known that the distinction between them is this. Then if speech is negated from Him, the defect of impairment like incapacity and muteness would be entailed, so it is from the attributes of essence.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof. It presents two criteria used by different groups to distinguish between attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fiʿl). The first criterion is based on whether the attribute can be described along with its opposite: if an attribute is such that both it and its opposite cannot be described of God, it is an attribute of essence (e.g., life vs. death). If an attribute can be described but its opposite cannot, it is an attribute of action (e.g., giving life vs. giving death is not a true opposite). The second criterion, used by the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, is based on consequence: if negating the attribute entails a defect (naqīṣa) in God, it is an attribute of essence; if negation does not entail a defect, it is an attribute of action. The passage then applies this to divine speech (al-kalām): negating speech would entail the defect of incapacity or muteness, therefore speech is an attribute of essence.

Key Terms
نقيصة
الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if an attribute is not eternal, it must be an action, but speech is shown to be essential despite being temporal in manifestation.
Correction: The defect criterion shows speech is essential because its negation would be a defect, even though its manifestation can be temporal.

Checkpoint
According to the Ahl al-Hadith mutakallimun, why is 'speech' considered an attribute of essence?
A) Because God spoke to Moses.
B) Because negating speech would imply a defect like muteness.
C) Because speech is eternal.
D) Because speech has no opposite.

Key Takeaway
The defect criterion provides a logical basis for distinguishing essential attributes from actions.

The passage pairs each attribute with its opposite defect. Think of a time you attributed a defect to God (even inadvertently) through doubt or ignorance. What specific step will you take to replace that doubt with certainty in His perfect attributes?

The Eternity of All Attributes and Takwīn
Nasafi declares all attributes eternal and argues for takwīn as an eternal meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that all divine attributes are eternal, and specifically the attribute of takwīn as an eternal meaning distinct from creation.

Core Idea
All of Allah’s attributes are eternal, including takwīn, which is not the created thing.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi asserts a key Maturidi doctrine: there is no need to separate attributes into eternal and temporal because all are eternal. He then focuses on the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence) to clarify that it is an eternal attribute subsisting in God’s essence, not identical to the things created.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp Nasafi’s statement.
Notice the bracketed title; it is part of the passage.
2
Understand the context
Nasafi is responding to those who distinguish between attributes of essence (eternal) and attributes of action (temporal). He rejects that distinction entirely.
3
Focus on takwīn
Why does Nasafi say takwīn is a meaning (maʿnā) beyond the created thing? This is crucial for the Maturidi defense of eternal creation.
Takwīn is eternal; the created thing is temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الصفات كلها أزلية عند النسفي]: ونحن لا حاجة بنا إلى إثبات الفرق لأنها عندنا كلها أزلية. فنحتاج إلى الكلام في كونه خالقا في الأزل، وفي إثبات صفة التكوين الله تعالى في الأزل قائمة بذاته، وأنها معنى وراء المكون.
[All attributes are eternal according to al-Nasafi]: And we have no need to prove the distinction, because according to us they are all eternal. So we need to discuss His being Creator in eternity, and to affirm the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence) for God, exalted, in eternity, subsisting in His essence, and that it is a meaning beyond the thing brought into existence.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is a statement of doctrine. Nasafi declares that he and his school (Maturidis) do not need to prove the distinction between attributes of essence and action because they hold that all attributes are eternal. Instead, the focus shifts to the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence): it must be established that God is Creator (khāliq) in eternity, that takwīn is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, and that it is a distinct meaning (maʿnā) separate from the created thing (al-mukawwan). This sets up the Maturidi position against those who deny an eternal attribute of creation.

The Eternity of All Attributes Including Takwin
Nasafi states all attributes eternal, takwin distinct from created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that all divine attributes, including takwin, are eternal and that takwin is a distinct attribute from the created thing.

Core Idea
Takwin is an eternal attribute of God, not identical to what it creates.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi articulates a key Maturidi doctrine: all of God's attributes are eternal, including the attribute of bringing into being (takwin). He clarifies that takwin subsists in God's essence and is distinct from the created thing. This lesson will unpack that claim and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let Nasafi's own words establish the point before you interpret.
Notice the two sentences: the first states no need to prove difference, the second introduces the need to discuss takwin.
2
Identify the core claim
Nasafi says all attributes are eternal ('كلها أزلية'). This is the foundation. Then he focuses on the attribute of takwin, asserting it is eternal and subsisting in God's essence.
This distinguishes the Maturidi view from those who see some attributes as temporal.
3
Understand takwin as distinct
Nasafi states that takwin is a meaning (معنى) beyond the created thing (المكون). This means the attribute is not the same as the thing brought into being; it is a separate eternal attribute.
This avoids the misconception that takwin is identical to the creation.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider why this matters: if takwin were temporal, God would not be Creator in pre‑eternity. By making it eternal, Maturidi theology preserves God's eternal creative power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن لا حاجة بنا إلى إثبات الفرق لأنها عندنا كلها أزلية. فنحتاج إلى الكلام في كونه خالقا في الأزل، وفي إثبات صفة التكوين الله تعالى في الأزل قائمة بذاته، وأنها معنى وراء المكون.
And we have no need to prove the difference because according to us they are all eternal. So we need to discuss His being a Creator in pre-eternity, and to establish the attribute of bringing into being (al-takwin) of God Most High in pre-eternity subsisting in His essence, and that it is a meaning beyond the created thing (al-mukawwan).
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Maturidi position on the eternity of God's attributes. The author begins by saying that he does not need to prove a distinction between different types of attributes (such as attributes of essence versus attributes of action) because all attributes are eternal. Then he identifies the specific need: to discuss God's being a Creator in pre-eternity (al-azal). This leads to establishing the attribute of 'bringing into being' (al-takwin) as an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence. He clarifies that this attribute is a meaning (ma'na) distinct from the thing that is brought into being (al-mukawwan). Thus, the attribute of takwin is eternal, while the mukawwan is created in time.

Correction: Nasafi clarifies that takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from the created thing (al-mukawwan), so it is not created and not identical to what it brings into being.

The Second Objection: Act and Object as Necessary Concomitants
Nasafi reports the second objection and announces his response strategy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the second objection against the eternity of takwin and how Nasafi prepares to refute it.

Core Idea
An eternal act would require an eternal object, so takwin cannot be eternal if the world is created.

In this passage, Nasafi presents the second objection raised by his opponents: if takwin (bringing into being) is eternal, then its object (mukawwan) must also be eternal, because an act and its effect are inseparable. He then begins outlining his response, stating that he will discuss the matter in four stages.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Carefully read the Arabic and translation of the objection. Notice the logical structure: premise, analogy, conclusion.
The objection uses everyday examples like striking and breaking.
2
Analyze the analogies
Identify the three analogies (striking/struck, breaking/broken, wounding/wounded) and understand why they are used to show that act and object are necessarily simultaneous.
3
Grasp the logical conclusion
The objection concludes that eternal takwin implies an eternal world, which is impossible. Therefore, takwin cannot be eternal.
This is the core of the objection.
4
See Nasafi's response plan
Nasafi declares he will speak about both aspects and debate each opponent. He then introduces the first topic: the discussion with those who say takwin and mukawwan are identical.
He mentions that the debate will cover four points.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني: أنهم يقولون لو كان التكوين ثابتا في الأزل، وكان الله تعالى مكونا خالقا للعالم، لكان المكون موجودا مخلوقا في الأزل، لما أن وجود الضرب ولا مضروب، ووجود الكسر ولا مكسور، ووجود الجرح ولا مجروح محال، فكان الفعل مع المفعول متلازمين، ولا يتصور ثبوت أحدهما بدون الآخر، فكان القول بوجود التكوين ولا مكون كالقول بوجود المكون ولا تكوين، وذلك محال فكذا هذا. ونحن نتكلم في الفصلين جميعا، ونناظر كل مخالف لنا على وجه يظهر لمن أنصف بطلان مقالته، ويثبت عنده صحة ما ذهبنا إليه - إن شاء الله تعالى. التكوين غير المكون]: فنبدأ أولا بالكلام مع من يقول: أن التكوين والمكون واحد. ويقع الكلام بيننا وبين الخصوم في مواضع أربعة.
And the second way: that they say: if bringing into being (al-takwin) were established in pre-eternity, and God Most High were a bringer into being and creator of the world, then the thing brought into being (al-mukawwan) would exist and be created in pre-eternity, because the existence of striking without a thing struck, and the existence of breaking without a thing broken, and the existence of wounding without a thing wounded is impossible. So the act and the object are necessary concomitants, and the establishment of one without the other cannot be conceived. So the statement of the existence of bringing into being without a thing brought into being is like the statement of the existence of a thing brought into being without bringing into being, and that is impossible, so this is likewise. And we will speak about both chapters together, and we will debate every opponent against us in a way that makes clear to whoever is just the falsehood of his statement, and establishes in his mind the correctness of what we have gone to – God willing. [Section: al-takwin is other than al-mukawwan]: So we begin first with the discussion with those who say: that al-takwin and al-mukawwan are one. And the discussion between us and the opponents occurs in four places.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection and the beginning of Nasafi's response. The objection is logical: if takwin (bringing into being) is eternal, then its object (mukawwan) must also be eternal, because an action and its object are necessarily simultaneous – like striking and something struck. The opponents argue that the existence of takwin without a mukawwan is as impossible as the existence of a mukawwan without takwin. Since the world is created and not eternal, takwin cannot be eternal. Nasafi then begins his reply. He announces that he will discuss both aspects (the two objections) and refute every opponent. Then he introduces the first topic: he will first address those who claim that takwin and mukawwan are identical. He states that the discussion with the opponents will cover four points. This sets up the subsequent detailed refutation. The passage is a transition from reporting the objection to outlining the response.

Key Terms

المكون
الأزل
متلازمين
الفعل
المفعول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if takwin is eternal, then the world must be eternal.
Correction: Nasafi will later show that takwin is eternal while its temporal objects are created in time. The concomitance is logical, but the object's existence depends on the act's temporal application, not the act's eternal existence.

Checkpoint

A) God cannot be a creator in pre-eternity.
B) An eternal act requires an eternal object.
C) Takwin is not a real attribute.

Key Takeaway
The second objection uses the necessary concomitance between act and object to argue against eternal takwin, but Nasafi prepares to refute it by distinguishing takwin from its temporal effects.

The Second Argument: Inseparability of Takwin and Mukawwan
Presents the second argument of the opponents and the author's intention to refute it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument used by those who equate takwin (bringing into existence) with mukawwan (the thing brought into existence), including their analogies and reasoning.

Core Idea
The opponents argue that if takwin is eternal, the world must be eternal because act and object are inseparable.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the second argument from those who claim that divine takwin and the created world are one and the same. They rely on analogies from physical actions to argue that an attribute and its object cannot be separated in time. Understanding this argument is essential before we see how the Maturidi school refutes it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage in Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of the argument's flow and terminology.
Notice the repeated use of 'وجود الضرب ولا مضروب' etc.
2
Identify the analogies used
The opponents cite three analogies: striking-struck, breaking-broken, wounding-wounded. What do these examples illustrate?
They all show that an action cannot exist without an object.
3
Understand the logical conclusion
From the analogies, the opponents conclude that takwin and mukawwan are inseparable. If takwin is eternal, then mukawwan must also be eternal.
This leads to the conclusion that the world is eternal, which contradicts Islamic belief in creation ex nihilo.
4
Note the author's response
The author does not refute here but promises to address both aspects and debate opponents to show the falsehood of their position.
This sets up the subsequent lesson where the refutation is provided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني: أنهم يقولون لو كان التكوين ثابتا في الأزل، وكان الله تعالى مكونا خالقا للعالم، لكان المكون موجودا مخلوقا في الأزل، لما أن وجود الضرب ولا مضروب، ووجود الكسر ولا مكسور، ووجود الجرح ولا مجروح محال، فكان الفعل مع المفعول متلازمين، ولا يتصور ثبوت أحدهما بدون الآخر، فكان القول بوجود التكوين ولا مكون كالقول بوجود المكون ولا تكوين، وذلك محال فكذا هذا. ونحن نتكلم في الفصلين جميعا، ونناظر كل مخالف لنا على وجه يظهر لمن أنصف بطلان مقالته، ويثبت عنده صحة ما ذهبنا إليه - إن شاء الله تعالى.
And the second aspect: that they say: if takwin (bringing into existence) were established in eternity, and Allah Most High is the bringer into existence, the creator of the world, then the brought-into-existence would be existent, created in eternity, because existence of striking without something struck, existence of breaking without something broken, and existence of wounding without something wounded is impossible. Thus the act and the object acted upon are inseparable, and it is inconceivable that one of them be established without the other. So saying that there is takwin without a thing brought into existence is like saying there is a thing brought into existence without takwin, and that is impossible. So this (i.e., your claim) is likewise impossible. And we will speak about both chapters and debate every opponent in a way that reveals to whoever is fair the falsehood of his statement, and establishes the correctness of what we hold – if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage presents a key argument from those who claim that divine takwin (bringing into existence) and the thing brought into existence (mukawwan) are one and the same. The opponents argue that if takwin is an eternal attribute of God, and God is the creator of the world, then the created world must also be eternal. They cite analogies: one cannot conceive of striking without something struck, breaking without something broken, or wounding without something wounded. These examples are meant to show that an act and its object are necessarily simultaneous. They then conclude that just as one cannot have a strike without something struck, one cannot have takwin without a thing brought into existence. Therefore, if takwin is eternal, the world must be eternal. The author, following the Maturidi school, responds by stating that he will address both aspects (takwin and mukawwan) and debate each opponent thoroughly to demonstrate the invalidity of their position. He does not provide a full refutation here but promises a detailed discussion. The passage shows that the opponents rely on a metaphor of physical actions to assert a necessary link between the attribute and its object, which the author will later argue is not applicable to divine attributes.

Key Terms
تكوين
مكون
متلازمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If an attribute (takwin) is eternal, then its object (mukawwan) must also be eternal.
Correction: The author will argue that divine attributes are not like physical actions; in God, the attribute may be eternal while its effect is temporal.

Checkpoint

A) Sitting and standing

D) Creating and annihilating

Key Takeaway
The opponents argue that takwin and mukawwan are inseparable, so if takwin is eternal, the world is eternal; the author will refute this.

The opponents used physical actions like striking and breaking to argue that act and object must go together. In your daily life, you experience cause and effect as simultaneous. What attachment in your heart prevents you from accepting that Allah's actions are unlike any cause you know?

Ash'ari Proofs That Khalq Is Not an Essential Attribute
Ash'ari arguments from Quran and consensus that khalq refers to creation, not God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four Ash'ari arguments from Quran, juristic consensus, common usage, and takfir that prove 'khalq' is not an attribute of God's essence but refers to created things.

Core Idea
Khalq is not what God is; it is what God makes.

The Ash'ari school marshals several independent proofs to show that 'khalq' (creation) is not an eternal attribute of God. They draw from a Quranic verse about Iblis, the legal consensus on oaths, everyday language, and the grave ruling of takfir. This concise passage collects these arguments to settle a key debate in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get the flow of arguments.
Notice the passage begins with an ambiguous line – it likely refers to creation being described as greater or lesser.
2
Identify the four proofs
There are four distinct proofs: (1) Quranic verse about Iblis, (2) juristic consensus on oaths, (3) common usage of 'khalq' for creatures, (4) consensus on takfir. Find each one.
The second proof is the longest – it includes analogy with attributes like power and knowledge.
3
Understand the oath analogy
The key point: swearing by 'khalq Allah' does not make an oath binding, unlike swearing by 'qudra Allah' or 'ilm Allah'. This shows 'khalq' is not an essential attribute.
Essential attributes are those that cannot be separated from God's essence.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
All arguments converge on the same point: 'khalq' refers to created things, not an attribute of God. The final argument about takfir shows the gravity of denying this.
The passage ends by equating denial with disbelief (kufr).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوصف بالأكبر والأصغر. وقوله تعالى خبرا عن إبليس عليه اللعنة: فليغيرنَ خَلَقَ اللهِ وما جاز عليه التغيير كان مخلوقا. وبهذه الآيات استدل بعض الأشعرية، قال: والدليل عليه إجماع الفقهاء أن من حلف بصفة من صفات ذات الباري جل وعلا انعقدت يمينه، ولو أنه قال: وخلق الله لا يكون يمينا، كما لو قال: ومخلوق الله ولو كان الخلق من صفات الذات لانعقدت به اليمين كما تنعقد بقوله: وقدرة الله وعلم الله. قال: وكذا الناس أجمعوا على إطلاق القول: بأن الله تعالى خالق الخلق، ويقولون: يرحم الله هذا الخلق، ويقولون: اللهم اصرف البلاء عن الخلق، وفرج الخلق عن هذا الغم، ويقولون: رسول الله خير الخلق، ويقولون: رأيت الخلق الكثير، وإن الخلق ازدحموا على كذا - ولعل إطلاق هذا الاسم في عرف اللسان وفي عرف الشرع وإجماع الأمة على المخلوقات أكثر من إطلاق اسم المخلوقات فمن ادعى بعد هذا أن هذا مجاز في الاستعمال لم ينفصل ممن يقول له: بل المخلوق مجاز في الاستعمال. ولأنهم أجمعوا على إكفار من امتنع عن القول بأن الخلق غير الله تعالى، وأن الله تعالى ليس بخالق للخلق كما لو امتنع عن القول بأن الله تعالى خالق المخلوقات.
It is described as greater and smaller. And His statement, may He be exalted, telling about Iblis, upon him the curse: 'They will certainly change Allah's creation.' And whatever is subject to change is created. By these verses some Ash'aris argued. He said: The evidence for it is the consensus of the jurists that whoever takes an oath by an attribute of the essence of the Exalted Lord, his oath is binding. And if he said: 'By the creation of Allah' it would not be an oath, just as if he said: 'By the created thing of Allah'. And if creation were from the attributes of the essence, the oath would be binding with it as it is binding with His saying: 'By the power of Allah' and 'By the knowledge of Allah'. He said: Likewise, the people have unanimously agreed upon using the expression: that Allah, may He be exalted, is the Creator of creation, and they say: May Allah have mercy on this creation, and they say: O Allah, turn away affliction from the creation, and relieve the creation from this distress, and they say: The Messenger of Allah is the best of creation, and they say: I saw many creatures, and the creatures crowded over such-and-such. Perhaps the usage of this noun in the custom of the tongue and in the custom of the law and the consensus of the Ummah upon created things is more than the usage of the noun 'created things'. So whoever claims after this that this is metaphorical usage does not separate himself from someone who says to him: Rather, 'created thing' is metaphorical in usage. And because they unanimously agree upon declaring disbelief of whoever refrains from saying that creation is other than Allah, and that Allah, may He be exalted, is not the creator of creation, just as if he refrained from saying that Allah, may He be exalted, is the Creator of created things.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage presents a series of arguments from the Ash'ari school to demonstrate that 'khalq' (creation) is not an attribute of God's essence but rather refers to the created world. The passage begins with an ambiguous statement that 'it is described as greater and lesser', likely referring to creation itself being subject to degrees. The first proof is from the Quranic verse about Iblis vowing to change Allah's creation, implying that whatever can be changed is created, so creation itself is not eternal. The second proof is from the consensus (ijma') of jurists: if someone swears by an essential attribute like power or knowledge, the oath is binding; but if he swears by 'Allah's creation', it is not binding, just as swearing by a created thing is not binding. If creation were an essential attribute, it would be treated like power or knowledge. The third proof is from common usage: people naturally use the word 'khalq' to refer to creatures, and this usage is more frequent than using 'makhluq'. The widespread consensus on this usage indicates that 'khalq' is not an attribute of God. The fourth proof is from the consensus on takfir: the community agrees on excommunicating those who deny that 'khalq' is other than God, meaning that considering creation as part of God's essence is disbelief. Together, these proofs show that 'khalq' is a created thing, not an eternal attribute.

Misconception: The word 'khalq' always means the act of creating (an attribute of God).
Correction: The passage shows that 'khalq' predominantly refers to the created thing, not the act, based on usage, oaths, and consensus.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari proofs establish that 'khalq' is a created thing, not an eternal attribute of God's essence.

Ash'ari Doubts on Takwin as a Distinct Attribute
Ash'ari rational arguments that takwin is temporal and not a distinct attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key rational arguments from the Ash'ari school that challenge the Maturidi doctrine of takwin as an eternal attribute separate from power.

Core Idea
If takwin were distinct from power, God would have two powers, which is impossible.

The Ash'ari school raises several rational objections against the Maturidi position that takwin (bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute distinct from power (qudra). These arguments aim to show that takwin would be redundant, lead to absurdities, or serve no purpose. In this passage, we examine the primary logical proofs that Ash'aris use to deny takwin as a separate attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
The passage presents rational doubts from the Ash'aris. First, read the Arabic and translation to get the overall argument. Notice that the main claim is that takwin cannot be a separate attribute.
2
Examine the first argument: two powers
The first point is that if khalq (creation) were a separate attribute, it would be another power, leading to two powers in God, which is impossible. Understand why this is a reductio ad absurdum.
This is a key objection.
3
Analyze the second argument: sufficiency of power
The second argument states that if God's power encompasses all possible things, then He has no need for a separate attribute of creation. Takwin would be redundant.
4
Consider the third argument: lack of benefit
The third argument says that affirming an attribute without benefit is pointless—its existence and non-existence are equal. Takwin does not fit the two rational categories of attributes (action-indicating or deficiency-negating).
This connects to the broader theory of attributes.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Bring all three arguments together. The Ash'aris conclude that takwin cannot be an eternal attribute because it leads to contradictions or uselessness. How would a Maturidi respond?
This prepares for deeper study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه عقلية للأشاعرة تثبت حدوث التكوين وأنه ليس صفة زائدة على القدرة: ومن جهة المعقول أن عند هؤلاء القوم أن المخلوق واقع بالخلق، فيلزمهم أن يكون الخلق بمعنى القدرة، ولو كان كذلك للزم أن يكون الله تعالى قدرتان، وهذا محال ولأن قدرة الباري إن كانت شاملة لجميع المقدورات استغنى عن الخلق والإيجاد، ولا يجوز إثبات صفة الله تعالى لا فائدة فيها، لأن ما لا فائدة في وجوده فوجوده وعدمه سواء، وإثبات صفة الله تعالى يكون وجودها وعدمها سواء كان إثباتها كنفيها، يدل عليه أن الصفات التي يمكن إثباتها الله تعالى عقلا، أن تكون من مدلولات الفعل كالحياة، أو لنفي نقص عن الذات لا ينتفي إلا بإثباته كالسمع
Rational doubts of the Ash'aris establishing the temporality of takwin and that it is not an additional attribute to power: And from the perspective of reason, according to these people, the created thing occurs by creation (khalq). So it follows that creation is in the sense of power. And if that were the case, it would necessitate that Allah, may He be exalted, has two powers, and that is impossible. And because the power of the Exalted, if it encompasses all possible things, He is independent of creation and bringing into existence. And it is not permissible to affirm an attribute of Allah, may He be exalted, without benefit in it, because what has no benefit in its existence, its existence and non-existence are equal. And affirming an attribute of Allah whose existence and non-existence are equal is like negating it. Evidence for this is that the attributes that can be affirmed for Allah, may He be exalted, rationally are either from the indications of action like life, or for negating a deficiency from the essence that is not negated except by affirming it like hearing.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage presents rational objections (shubah aqliyya) from the Ash'ari school to prove that takwin (bringing into existence) is temporal and not an additional attribute separate from power (qudra). The argument begins by noting that according to the Ash'aris, the created thing comes about by 'khalq' (creation). If khalq is a separate attribute, it would effectively be another power, resulting in two powers in God, which is impossible. Moreover, if God's power already encompasses all possible things, He has no need of a separate attribute for creation. It is not permissible to affirm an attribute of God that serves no benefit, because its existence and non-existence would be equivalent. The attributes that can be rationally affirmed for God are of two types: those that indicate action (like life) and those that negate a deficiency (like hearing). Takwin does not fall into either category, so it should not be affirmed as an eternal attribute. This passage thus refutes the idea that khalq or takwin is an additional eternal attribute distinct from power.

صفات

Correction: The passage argues that creation is an act of power, not a separate attribute. Affirming a distinct attribute of creation would be equivalent to affirming a second power, which is impossible.

Key Takeaway

Proving Action Cannot Be Eternal
Nasafi proves by logical division that action cannot be eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses logical division to prove that action cannot be eternal.

Core Idea
To prove action is not eternal, examine the predicate-object relationship.

Nasafi tackles a key challenge in understanding divine attributes: can an action be eternal? He constructs a logical argument using division of possibilities. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the starting point
The determined thing (maqdur) is non-existent in eternity. This is the premise.
The maqdur is what is determined by an action.
2
Recognize the analogy
Some predicates extend to both existent and non-existent subjects, like 'knowing' (عالم) and 'having knowledge' (له علم).
3
Apply the division to action
Consider the action: either the predicate (what extends) is existent in eternity while its object is non-existent, or both are existent or both non-existent.
These are the only logical possibilities.
4
Draw the contradiction
If the predicate is eternal and object non-existent, the subject (knower) must be eternal. If both existent and non-existent, both attributes would be necessary, which is impossible.
5
Conclude the argument
All divisions are invalidated, so action cannot be eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شك أن المقدور معدوم في الأزل وإما ما يتعدى إلى الموجود والمعدوم كقولنا: عالم وله علم. فلا يخلو ما نحن فيه من الفعل إما أن يكون ما يتعدى موجودا في الأزل والمعتدي إليه معدوما، ولو كان كذلك لاقتضى أن يكون العالم موجودا في الأزل، إن كان موجودا ومعدوما لزم الأمران جميعا. وإذا بطلت هذه الأقسام ثبت بطلان وجود الفعل في الأزل.
The doubt that the determined (maqdur) is non-existent in eternity, and sometimes it extends to the existent and the non-existent, like our saying: knowing and having knowledge. So our subject of the action (fi'l) is not free: either that which extends is existent in eternity and that which is extended to is non-existent, and if it were so, it would require that the knower be existent in eternity; if it were existent and non-existent, both attributes would be necessary. And when these divisions are invalidated, the invalidity of the existence of action in eternity is established.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a proof that action (fi'l) cannot be eternal. It begins by stating a doubt: the determined thing (maqdur) is non-existent in eternity. Then it notes that some predicates extend to both existent and non-existent, like 'knowing' (aam) and 'having knowledge' (lahu ilm). Then it applies a tripartite division to the action under discussion: either (a) the predicate extends from something existent in eternity to something non-existent, (b) or something else. The reasoning shows that certain consequences lead to a contradiction, thereby proving that action cannot be eternal. The author proceeds systematically by dividing possibilities and eliminating them.

Key Terms
مقدور (maqdur)
فعل (fi'l)
أزل (azal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the consequence if the predicate (what extends) is existent in eternity while the object (what is extended to) is non-existent?
A) The subject must be non-existent.
B) The subject must be existent in eternity.
C) Both attributes become impossible.
D) The action becomes eternal.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi proves that action cannot be eternal by showing that all logical divisions lead to contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If action cannot be eternal because it requires a temporal object, then your own actions are anchored in time. Are you using your finite moments for what truly matters in eternity? What is one action you will change today because you realize it will not last forever?
?
Nasafi argues that an eternal action with a temporal object is incoherent. Your deeds are temporal, but their effects may reach beyond. Which of your daily habits are you building as if they will endure forever, despite their temporality? How will you shift focus to actions that have eternal value?
?
The proof that action is not eternal shows that only God's essence is independent of time. Do you live as if your actions are the ultimate source of your worth, or do you anchor your identity in the Eternal? What is one fear you have about your finite life that this proof calls you to surrender?

Ash'ari Arguments Against Takwin as an Attribute
Ash'ari rational proofs against takwin as an additional attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational arguments the Ash'aris use to deny that takwin is a separate eternal attribute of Allah.

Core Idea
Takwin cannot be distinct from qudra without implying multiple powers or useless attributes.

The Ash'aris argue that if creation (takwin) were a distinct attribute, it would either duplicate power or be superfluous. This lesson presents those rational proofs, setting the stage for the Maturidi refutation. Read carefully to see how each argument builds on the previous one.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the structure: three distinct arguments are presented.
The first argument concerns the relationship between khalq and qudra.
2
Identify the three arguments
Find where each argument begins. The first argues that if khalq is distinct, Allah would have two powers. The second argues that encompassing power makes creation unnecessary. The third argues that an attribute without benefit is invalid.
3
Reflect on the logic
Consider why each argument is presented. The Ash'aris aim to show that takwin cannot be an additional attribute because it leads to absurdity or uselessness.
This reasoning is a form of reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه عقلية للأشاعرة تثبت حدوث التكوين وأنه ليس صفة زائدة على القدرة: ومن جهة المعقول أن عند هؤلاء القوم أن المخلوق واقع بالخلق، فيلزمهم أن يكون الخلق بمعنى القدرة، ولو كان كذلك للزم أن يكون الله تعالى قدرتان، وهذا محال ولأن قدرة الباري إن كانت شاملة لجميع المقدورات استغنى عن الخلق والإيجاد، ولا يجوز إثبات صفة الله تعالى لا فيها، لأن ما لا فائدة في وجوده فوجوده وعدمه سواء، وإثبات صفة الله تعالى يكون وجودها وعدمها سواء كان إثباتها كنفيها، يدل عليه أن الصفات التي يمكن إثباتها الله تعالى عقلا، أن تكون من مدلولات الفعل كالحياة، أو لنفي نقص عن الذات لا ينتفي إلا بإثباته كالسمع والبصر والكلام، ثم الفعل إذا لم يكن له تعلق بالمفعول، إذ جميع المفعولات حاصلة بالقدرة ولم يكن إثباته لنفي نقص لا ينتفي إلا به لم يجز إثباته.
Rational doubts for the Ash'aris establishing the origination of takwin and that it is not an additional attribute over qudra: From the aspect of reason: according to these people, the created thing occurs by creation (khalq), so it follows for them that creation is in the sense of power (qudra). If it were so, it would follow that Allah has two powers, and this is impossible. And because if the power of the Almighty encompasses all determined things, He would be free from need of creation and bringing into existence. And it is not permissible to establish an attribute of Allah in which there is no benefit, because whatever has no benefit in its existence, its existence and non-existence are equal. And establishing an attribute of Allah whose existence and non-existence are equal is like establishing it and negating it. This is indicated by the fact that the attributes which can be established for Allah rationally are either from the implications of action like life, or for negation of deficiency from the essence that is not negated except by establishing it, like hearing, sight, and speech. Then if an action (fi'l) has no relation to the object of action (maf'ul), since all objects of action are produced by power, and its establishment is not for negation of a deficiency that is not negated except by it, it is not permissible to establish it.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage presents a rational argument from the Ash'aris against the Maturidi belief that takwin (bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute distinct from qudra (power). The argument proceeds in steps: first, if creation (khalq) is the means by which the created occurs, then khalq must be identical to qudra, otherwise there would be two powers. Second, if qudra is all-encompassing, then there is no need for an additional attribute of creation. Third, an attribute with no benefit should not be posited. The passage then gives a Maturidi response (likely the author's own view) that attributes are only established for two reasons: either they are implications of action (like life) or they negate a deficiency (like hearing). Since the action (fi'l) is not related to the object (all objects are already produced by qudra) and does not negate a deficiency, it cannot be established as an attribute. Thus the Maturidi refutes the need for a separate attribute of takwin.

Key Terms
تكوين (takwin)
خلق (khalq)
قدرة (qudra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ash'aris deny that Allah creates or that creation is an act of Allah.
Correction: The Ash'aris affirm that Allah creates, but they identify creation (khalq) with the attribute of power (qudra), not as a separate attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari argument, what would be the consequence if creation (khalq) is considered a meaning distinct from power (qudra)?
A) Allah would have two powers.
B) Allah would be unable to create.
C) Creation would be eternal.
D) The created would be uncreated.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'aris argue that takwin cannot be a separate attribute because it would either duplicate power or be useless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How does the Ash'ari argument that creation is identical to power challenge your sense of personal responsibility? Will you reconsider how you attribute your successes and failures to yourself versus Allah?
?
The passage says that an attribute with no benefit should not be established. Have you ever held a belief about Allah that had no real benefit for your faith or practice? What would it mean for you to let go of such a belief today, even if it felt familiar?
?
If Allah's power is sufficient for all creation, then nothing is outside His control. Where in your life do you act as if something is beyond His power? Will you surrender that area to Him right now?

Maturidi Response: The Criterion for Divine Attributes
Maturidi criterion for establishing divine attributes and its application to takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi criterion for establishing divine attributes and why takwin fails to meet it.

Core Idea
Attributes are only established if they imply action or negate a deficiency; takwin does neither.

The Maturidi response provides a principled criterion for which attributes can be affirmed of Allah. Attributes are either implications of action (like life) or negations of deficiencies (like hearing). Since takwin has no relation to the object and does not negate a deficiency, it cannot be established as an attribute. This refutes the Ash'ari position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Maturidi passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two categories of attributes mentioned.
The passage starts with 'يدل عليه' indicating this is a supporting argument.
2
Understand the two categories
First category: attributes that are implications of action, like life. Second: attributes that negate a deficiency, like hearing and sight.
These are the only valid reasons to posit an attribute.
3
Apply to takwin
The passage then argues that takwin does not relate to the object (since all objects are produced by power) and does not negate any deficiency, so it cannot be established.
This completes the refutation.

Source Text

Rational doubts for the Ash'aris establishing the origination of takwin and that it is not an additional attribute over qudra: From the aspect of reason: according to these people, the created thing occurs by creation (khalq), so it follows for them that creation is in the sense of power (qudra).
